<p>Wakefield's oldest church is All Saints, now <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Cathedral" title="Wakefield Cathedral">Wakefield Cathedral</a>, a 14th-century parish church built on the site of earlier Saxon and Norman churches, restored by Sir <a href="/wiki/George_Gilbert_Scott" title="George Gilbert Scott">George Gilbert Scott</a> in the 19th&#160;century, and raised to cathedral status in 1888. The first <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Wakefield_(diocese)" title="Bishop of Wakefield (diocese)">Bishop of Wakefield</a> was <a href="/wiki/William_Walsham_How" class="mw-redirect" title="William Walsham How">William Walsham How</a>.
In 1356 the <a href="/wiki/Chantry_Chapel_of_St_Mary_the_Virgin,_Wakefield" title="Chantry Chapel of St Mary the Virgin, Wakefield">Chantry Chapel of St Mary the Virgin</a> on Wakefield bridge was built originally in wood, and later in stone. This chapel is one of four chantry chapels built around Wakefield and the oldest and most ornate of the four surviving in England.<sup id="cite_ref-Historic_Wakefield_1066-1600_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historic_Wakefield_1066-1600-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bridge_Chapels_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bridge_Chapels-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
Wakefield is also known for the <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Cycle" class="mw-redirect" title="Wakefield Cycle">Wakefield Cycle</a>, a collection of 32 <a href="/wiki/Mystery_play" title="Mystery play">mystery plays</a>, dating from the 14th&#160;century, which were performed as part of the summertime religious festival of <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi_(feast)" title="Corpus Christi (feast)">Corpus Christi</a> and revived in recent times.<sup id="cite_ref-MysteryPlays_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MysteryPlays-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>St John's Church was built in 1795 in the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian</a> style. Three new Anglican <a href="/wiki/Commissioners%27_church" title="Commissioners&#39; church">Commissioners' churches</a>, partly financed by the "Million Fund" were built as chapels of ease in the surrounding districts and were St Peter at Stanley in 1824, St Paul at Alverthorpe in 1825, and St James at Thornes in 1831.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MillionAct_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MillionAct-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Holy Trinity in George Street was built in 1838-9.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> St Andrew's Church opened on Peterson Road in 1846 and St Mary's Church on Charles Street was consecrated in 1864. St Michael's was consecrated in 1861.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Westgate Unitarian Chapel dates from 1752. In the 19th&#160;century Wesleyan, Primitive and Independent Methodist chapels were opened and the Baptists opened a chapel in George Street in 1844.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Churchpics_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Churchpics-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/William_Swinden_Barber#Church_of_St_John_the_Divine,_Calder_Grove,_1892" title="William Swinden Barber">St John the Divine</a> was built at Calder Grove in 1892.<sup id="cite_ref-LT_27_May_1893_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LT_27_May_1893-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">diocese</a> of Wakefield covered parishes mainly in West Yorkshire, parts of South Yorkshire and five parishes in North Yorkshire.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> It was dissolved on Easter Sunday 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Platten" title="Stephen Platten">Stephen Platten</a> was the 12th and last <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Wakefield_(diocese)" title="Bishop of Wakefield (diocese)">Bishop of Wakefield</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Diocese_of_Leeds" title="Anglican Diocese of Leeds">Diocese of Leeds</a><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> now covers Wakefield.
</p><p>Wakefield has two Catholic parishes - in the north <a href="/wiki/St_Martin_de_Porres" class="mw-redirect" title="St Martin de Porres">St Martin de Porres</a> incorporates the churches of <a href="/wiki/St_Austin%27s_Church,_Wakefield" title="St Austin&#39;s Church, Wakefield">St Austin's</a>, Wentworth Terrace, opened in 1828, and English Martyrs, opened in 1932, on Dewsbury Road, Lupset,<sup id="cite_ref-St_Austins_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St_Austins-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> and in the south, St Peter and St Paul's off Standbridge Lane which has a modern church built in 1991. Wakefield is in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Leeds" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Leeds">Roman Catholic Diocese of Leeds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Agbrigg Muslim Association have a Zakaria Masjid Mosque in Wakefield.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wakefield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_ruins_of_Sandal_Castle1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/The_ruins_of_Sandal_Castle1.JPG/220px-The_ruins_of_Sandal_Castle1.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/The_ruins_of_Sandal_Castle1.JPG/330px-The_ruins_of_Sandal_Castle1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/The_ruins_of_Sandal_Castle1.JPG/440px-The_ruins_of_Sandal_Castle1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_ruins_of_Sandal_Castle1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The ruins of <a href="/wiki/Sandal_Castle" title="Sandal Castle">Sandal Castle</a></div></div></div>
<p>The ruins of <a href="/wiki/Sandal_Castle" title="Sandal Castle">Sandal Castle</a> and its visitor centre are open to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Royal,_Wakefield" title="Theatre Royal, Wakefield">Theatre Royal Wakefield</a> on Westgate, designed by architect <a href="/wiki/Frank_Matcham" title="Frank Matcham">Frank Matcham</a> opened in 1894 and currently presents a programme of entertainment including musicals, drama, live music, stand up comedy and dance.<sup id="cite_ref-theatreroyalwakefield_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theatreroyalwakefield-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Wakefield's two central libraries closed and moved into the £31&#160;million Wakefield One in October 2012. The new library was officially opened by singer <a href="/wiki/Jarvis_Cocker" title="Jarvis Cocker">Jarvis Cocker</a> on 10 November 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Museum" title="Wakefield Museum">Wakefield Museum</a> moved from the former Mechanics' Institute on Wood Street to Wakefield One at the same time. The museum was officially opened by <a href="/wiki/David_Attenborough" title="David Attenborough">Sir David Attenborough</a> on 9 March 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
Balne Lane library managed a regional collection of more than 500,000 items of music and 90,000 copies of plays for Yorkshire Libraries &amp; Information (YLI).<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> The Yorkshire Music and Drama Library at Balne Lane closed on 31 March 2012 when the music section moved to Huddersfield and the drama section to Leeds.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Hepworth_Wakefield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1507085.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/The_Hepworth_Wakefield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1507085.jpg/220px-The_Hepworth_Wakefield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1507085.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/The_Hepworth_Wakefield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1507085.jpg/330px-The_Hepworth_Wakefield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1507085.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/The_Hepworth_Wakefield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1507085.jpg/440px-The_Hepworth_Wakefield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1507085.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Hepworth_Wakefield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1507085.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Hepworth_Wakefield" title="The Hepworth Wakefield">The Hepworth Wakefield</a> and the River Calder</div></div></div>
<p>In May 2011 the Hepworth Wakefield gallery opened on the south bank of the River Calder near Wakefield Bridge, displaying work by local artists Barbara Hepworth and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Moore" title="Henry Moore">Henry Moore</a> and other British and international artists. The gallery is thought to be the largest purpose-built gallery to open in the United Kingdom since 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-Gallery_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gallery-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The West Riding Registry of Deeds on Newstead Road is the headquarters of the West Yorkshire Archive Service, housing records from the former West Riding and West Yorkshire counties, and is the record office for the Wakefield Metropolitan District.<sup id="cite_ref-WYJS_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WYJS-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Wakefield's three contiguous parks have a history dating back to 1893 when Clarence Park opened on land near Lawe Hill. The adjacent Holmefield Estate was acquired in 1919, followed by Thornes House in 1924, making a large park to the south west of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-chatparks_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chatparks-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Park_Festival" title="Clarence Park Festival">Clarence Park Music Festival</a> is held annually in Clarence Park, promoting local bands.<sup id="cite_ref-CPMF_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPMF-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two children's <a href="/wiki/Nursery_rhymes" class="mw-redirect" title="Nursery rhymes">nursery rhymes</a> with Wakefield connections are "<a href="/wiki/Here_We_Go_Round_the_Mulberry_Bush" title="Here We Go Round the Mulberry Bush">Here We Go Round the Mulberry Bush</a>" which may have been sung by women inmates at Wakefield <a href="/wiki/Gaol" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaol">prison</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WP_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> and
"<a href="/wiki/The_Grand_Old_Duke_of_York" title="The Grand Old Duke of York">The Grand Old Duke of York</a>" which may allude to the Battle of Wakefield in 1460, referring to <a href="/wiki/Richard_Plantagenet,_3rd_Duke_of_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Plantagenet, 3rd Duke of York">Richard Plantagenet</a>, the 3rd Duke of York.<sup id="cite_ref-Historic_Wakefield_1066-1600_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historic_Wakefield_1066-1600-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>  The lyrics of the popular hymn "Onward Christian Soldiers" were written at St Peter's Church in nearby Horbury.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Wakefield is known as the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Rhubarb_Triangle" title="Rhubarb Triangle">Rhubarb Triangle</a>, an area notable for growing early forced <a href="/wiki/Rhubarb" title="Rhubarb">rhubarb</a>. In July 2005 a sculpture was erected to celebrate this facet of Wakefield, and there is an annual 'Wakefield Festival of Food, Drink and Rhubarb" which takes place over the last weekend in February.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rhubarb_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhubarb-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Wakefield's newspaper, the <i><a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Express" title="Wakefield Express">Wakefield Express</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-WEx_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WEx-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> was founded in 1852. Another newspaper, the <i>Wakefield Guardian</i> was established in 2007, but has ceased publishing.<sup id="cite_ref-WG_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WG-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Wakefield has a radio station, <a href="/wiki/Ridings_FM" title="Ridings FM">Ridings FM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rfm_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfm-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1913 Albert Winstanley opened the Picture House cinema in Westgate. Shortly after opening it was renamed the Playhouse, and by 1972 it was part of the Classic cinema chain. It is now a nightclub.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In 1935 <a href="/wiki/Associated_British_Cinemas" class="mw-redirect" title="Associated British Cinemas">Associated British Cinemas</a> (ABC) opened the Regal Cinema in Kirkgate. The <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> building was renamed the ABC in 1962 and became a <a href="/wiki/The_Cannon_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="The Cannon Group">Cannon</a> in 1986. <a href="/wiki/Cineworld" title="Cineworld">Cineworld</a>'s first purpose-built multiplex in Britain opened in Wakefield in December 1996. The ABC closed in 1997 and has remained derelict, but there have been successive proposals to redevelop or demolish it.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Coal_Mining_Museum_for_England" title="National Coal Mining Museum for England">National Coal Mining Museum for England</a> (an Anchor Point of ERIH, The <a href="/wiki/European_Route_of_Industrial_Heritage" title="European Route of Industrial Heritage">European Route of Industrial Heritage</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Sculpture_Park" title="Yorkshire Sculpture Park">Yorkshire Sculpture Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nostell_Priory" title="Nostell Priory">Nostell Priory</a><sup id="cite_ref-nostellpriory_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nostellpriory-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> are within the Wakefield metropolitan area, as is <a href="/wiki/Walton_Hall,_West_Yorkshire" title="Walton Hall, West Yorkshire">Walton Hall</a>, a Georgian mansion set in what was the world's first nature reserve, created by the explorer <a href="/wiki/Charles_Waterton" title="Charles Waterton">Charles Waterton</a>; the house is now a hotel.
</p><p>A small part of the 1977 BBC film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Price_of_Coal" title="The Price of Coal">The Price of Coal</a></i> was filmed in Wakefield with the Mines Rescue Team based in the city.  The end credits of the film give special thanks to the team.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wakefield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Trinity" title="Wakefield Trinity">Wakefield Trinity</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">Rugby League</a> club currently playing in the <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a>. The club, founded in 1873, was one of the initial founders of the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Northern Union</a> after the split from the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_Union" title="Rugby Football Union">Rugby Football Union</a> in 1895. The club plays at <a href="/wiki/Belle_Vue_(Wakefield)" title="Belle Vue (Wakefield)">Belle Vue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WTrinity_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WTrinity-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Several local teams play in different leagues of the <a href="/wiki/British_Amateur_Rugby_League_Association" title="British Amateur Rugby League Association">British Amateur Rugby League Association</a>, BARLA.
They include Wakefield City, Westgate Wolves, Crigglestone All Blacks, Kettlethorpe and Eastmoor Dragons.<sup id="cite_ref-BARLA_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BARLA-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rugby Union Football is played at <a href="/wiki/Sandal_RUFC" title="Sandal RUFC">Sandal RUFC</a><sup id="cite_ref-sandalrufc_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sandalrufc-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> and was played by <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_RFC" title="Wakefield RFC">Wakefield RFC</a> at <a href="/wiki/College_Grove_(Sports_Ground)" class="mw-redirect" title="College Grove (Sports Ground)">College Grove</a> from 1901 to 2004 when the club ceased to play.
</p><p>Wakefield briefly had a football team when <a href="/wiki/Emley_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Emley F.C.">Emley F.C.</a> moved to play at Belle Vue, the ground of Wakefield Trinity Wildcats.  After moving ground first to College Grove and then briefly to share with <a href="/wiki/Ossett_Town" class="mw-redirect" title="Ossett Town">Ossett Town</a>, Wakefield FC folded in June 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/AFC_Emley" class="mw-redirect" title="AFC Emley">AFC Emley</a> was founded to restore the club's original links with the village of Emley.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Wakefield Sports Club at College Grove also has the Yorkshire Regional Hockey Academy, Wakefield Bowls Club and Wakefield Squash Club on the same site.<sup id="cite_ref-WSC_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSC-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Wakefield Archers meet at QEGS in Wakefield or at Slazengers Sports Club, Horbury and has archers shooting Olympic re-curve bows, compound bows and longbows.<sup id="cite_ref-Archery_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archery-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
Thornes Park Athletics Stadium is home to Wakefield Harriers A.C. Members <a href="/wiki/Martyn_Bernard" title="Martyn Bernard">Martyn Bernard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emily_Freeman" title="Emily Freeman">Emily Freeman</a> competed in the Beijing Olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-WAC_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WAC-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
Local teams Newton Hill and Wakefield Thornes are members of the Leeds-West Riding Cricket League.<sup id="cite_ref-lwrcl_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lwrcl-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There is a 100-acre (0.40&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) watersports lake at <a href="/wiki/Pugneys_Country_Park" title="Pugneys Country Park">Pugneys Country Park</a> catering for non-powered watersports such as canoeing, sailing and windsurfing.<sup id="cite_ref-Pugneys_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pugneys-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Golf clubs include the municipal course at Lupset and the private Wakefield Golf Club at Sandal.<sup id="cite_ref-Golf_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Golf-152">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wakefield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wakefield_(HM_Prison)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wakefield (HM Prison)">Wakefield Prison</a>, originally built as a house of correction in 1594, is a maximum security prison.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Wakefield is policed by the West Yorkshire Police force and is within the DA, Wakefield division, which covers the whole district.<sup id="cite_ref-WYP_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WYP-154">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Wakefield is also the location of the West Yorkshire Police Force Headquarters, located on Laburnam Road. The <a href="/wiki/Fire_service_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Fire service in the United Kingdom">statutory emergency fire and rescue service</a> is provided by the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Fire_and_Rescue_Service" title="West Yorkshire Fire and Rescue Service">West Yorkshire Fire and Rescue Service</a>, from Wakefield fire station.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Hospital services are provided by the Mid Yorkshire Hospitals NHS Trust and community health services, including <a href="/wiki/General_Practitioner" class="mw-redirect" title="General Practitioner">GPs</a>, district and community nurses, dentists and pharmacists, are co-ordinated by Wakefield District <a href="/wiki/Primary_Care_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary Care Trust">Primary Care Trust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Waste_management" title="Waste management">Waste management</a> is co-ordinated by the <a href="/wiki/Local_authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Local authority">local authority</a>. Wakefield's <a href="/wiki/Distribution_Network_Operator" class="mw-redirect" title="Distribution Network Operator">Distribution Network Operator</a> for electricity is <a href="/wiki/CE_Electric_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="CE Electric UK">CE Electric</a> via <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Electricity" title="Yorkshire Electricity">Yorkshire Electricity</a>. <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Water" title="Yorkshire Water">Yorkshire Water</a> manages Wakefield's <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">drinking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waste_water" class="mw-redirect" title="Waste water">waste water</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wakefield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Wakefield" title="List of people from Wakefield">List of people from Wakefield</a></div>
<p>Novelist <a href="/wiki/George_Gissing" title="George Gissing">George Gissing</a> was born in Wakefield in 1857; his childhood home in Thompson's Yard is maintained by The Gissing Trust.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Sculptor <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Hepworth" title="Barbara Hepworth">Barbara Hepworth</a> was born in Wakefield in 1903.<sup id="cite_ref-BH_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BH-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> There is an art gallery called the Hepworth named after her which features her work alongside other local artists such as <a href="/wiki/Henry_Moore" title="Henry Moore">Henry Moore</a><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/David_Storey" title="David Storey">David Storey</a> born in Wakefield in 1933 was a <a href="/wiki/Novelist" title="Novelist">novelist</a> and playwright who in 1960 wrote <i><a href="/wiki/This_Sporting_Life" title="This Sporting Life">This Sporting Life</a></i>, which was made into a film in 1963 and shot largely on location in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-DS_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DS-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Former Archbishop of York, David Hope <a href="/wiki/David_Hope,_Baron_Hope_of_Thornes" title="David Hope, Baron Hope of Thornes">The Rt Revd and Rt Hon The Lord Hope of Thornes</a>  KCVO PC, was born in 1940 in Thornes.<sup id="cite_ref-DH_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DH-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/John_Leech_(politician)" title="John Leech (politician)">John Leech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrat</a> Leader of the Opposition on <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_Council" title="Manchester City Council">Manchester City Council</a>, was born in Wakefield in 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_cities">Twin cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wakefield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Twin cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wakefield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wakefield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Notes</b>
</p>

<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Wakefield's <i>thorpes</i> are: Alverthorpe, Chapelthorpe, Gawthorpe, Hollingthorpe, Kettlethorpe, Kirkthorpe, Milnthorpe, Ouchthorpe, Painthorpe, Snapethorpe, Woodthorpe, Wrenthorpe. Flanshaw, <a href="/wiki/Kirkhamgate" title="Kirkhamgate">Kirkhamgate</a>, Carrgate and Lupset have <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> origins.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"A very lively market town and suitably large, well served with fish and meat both from sea and by rivers... so that all food is very good and cheap there. A right honest man shall eat well for 2d a meal. There is plenty coal in the area around Wakefield."<sup id="cite_ref-Old_Wakefield_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Old_Wakefield-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
